Here is a really easy tip to check the temp of your oil - if you place the tip of a wooden spoon in the oil, and little bubbles form around it, the oil is ready to go.

text:
Ok, I have been searching a lot of different sites for a great friend chicken recipe and I finally found one.

I think the overall mixture make for a great crunchy texture, but I found the flavor to be a bit bland without the use of the dip.  I believer a good friend chicken should not have to be dipped (or chicken strips in my case)

I followed the recipe exactly (including the beer, I used my favorite Icehouse) anyways, I used Granulated Garlic instead of Garlic salt and after I tested my first piece I decided it needed more flavor.  In the batter I put 2 table spoons of All Season Salt and 1 table spoons of Celery Salt and WOW!  They are awesome to eat even without dip.

Anyways, I wanted to leave my .02 cents because this recipe really is very good and worth it.

text:
I tried this recipe after reading the reviews so I also doubled the spices, except for the black pepper. I also added a dash of tabasco to the wet ingredients. To boost the flavour of the chicken, I marinated it in buttermilk with garlic salt, poultry seasoning, and a dash of tabasco. Chicken was flavourful and moist and the coating was crispy and delicious. Make sure your oil is hot enough and, if you fry in batches that it comes back up to temp between batches. This will prevent greasy coating.

We recently made this recipe prior to a hurricane so that we would have something to eat after we lost power.  Several hours later, even after sitting on the counter, it was by far the most cripsy chicken I have ever eaten!  KFC's secret recipe has nothing on this one.  The spices were a little more salty than I like, but it was still a great tasting treat.  Next time I will use plain garlic instead of garlic salt, and maybe try some crushed red pepper or chili powder to bump up the spice.  This will definitley become a hurricane necessity along with bottle water and flashlights! Thanks for the post.

text:
To those who found the chicken bland, try soaking in buttermilk with salt, pepper and poultry seasoning or a buttermilk-ranch dressing mix for at least an hour, or defrost the chicken in this mix. Adds juiciness and flavour to the chicken. 1-2 tbsp of vinegar or lemon juice plus milk to make one cup is a great buttermilk substitute.

text:
I gave this recipe five stars because it's great for what it is and this may be the first time I've had the crispy part turn out similar to professionally made fried chicken, especially that it mostly sticks to skinless/boneless chicken breasts, and the meat itself was tender and tasty.  Bravo!

That said, I'm tempted to change up the recipe to give it more spunk: 1) Increase the spices somewhat, maybe substituting McCormicks' Montreal Chicken for the poultry seasoning and adding a bit of cayenne pepper.  2) Substitute corn meal for part of the flour.  3) Substitute milk for the water. 4) In the case of using skinless/boneless chicken, perhaps use the set-aside egg whites mixed with some milk for an initial coating to help with making the crispy coating stick better (yeap, this makes it quadruple-dipped!).  For the initial try, I only changed it to fry in shortening (the way my grandma did it), used water in place of beer, and because I thought I didn't have garlic salt, I combined garlic powder and salt.

This is pretty good fried chicken. I loved how thick the crust was on this. I only had boneless chicken breast, but wanted to try this recipe. I am sure the bone in would be great. For the 6 chicken breasts I cut all the ingredients in half including the cooking oil. I kept all the ingredients the same just cut the black pepper in half for personal choice. I thought the poultry seasoning gave it a nice flavor. I wish my chicken had a little more taste like the crust, but I could have seasoned the chicken to. It was skinless, so that probably didn't help. This is definitely a weekend type recipe, as it is kind of time-consuming. However, I have yet to see a fried chicken recipe that wasn't! TY

text:
I've made these twice since saving the recipe. The first time, I used 2 whole chickens with skin and bones, and the beer was a Boddington's Cream Ale (which is all we had but isn't anyone's favourite beer). The family were a little disappointed, as was I. A lot of work for not much flavour.

The second time I made it with skinless/boneless chicken breast, Newcastle Brown Ale (one of our preferred beers) and used garlic powder instead of garlic salt. The family LOVED this result and have asked for more.

The amount of liquid called for in the recipe makes a batter that is, IMO, a little too thick to work with, so I used 1.5 times the beer called for and was happy with the consistency, but the coating wasn't quite as crispy as it was when I first made it with the liquids as listed in the recipe.

All things considered, definitely a keeper.

Crunchy, but lacking immensely in flavour. I have a recipe given to me by a friend that is much better, though is less thick on the fried coating. I barely managed to eat a full piece... text:
Hi everyone, I have not tried this recipe yet, but I plan to! When reading other's reviews, they said the chicken was bland, well I have a fix for you... we brine every piece of meat before we do anything with it overnite.  place your chicken in a gallon plastic bag, add 1/4 cup salt, 1/4 cup sugar, 1/4 cup apple cider vinegar, about 10 peppercorns, 1 tbs poultry seasoning, fill bag with cold water, place in a bowl in the refrigerator overnight..drain dry and make your fried chicken! (or if you are from NYS - try the "cornell chicken marinade" I am sure you can find it online, but if you do use that marinade only brine 4-6 hrs. Hope you enjoy!

My family liked it, but next time I will use way more spices like others suggest. Adding the beer helped keep subsequent chicken pieces crispy and light. I also "sifted" out the doughy pieces that accumulated in the dry mix and that helped too.

text:
Made this today. I've never had luck with frying chicken. Either the center is too raw or the coating isn't good. But, this got an A+ from everyone at the table. I was worried that coating would be too spicy based on other comments so I used about half the pepper, but I wish I had used the whole amount because you couldn't taste it. The chicken breast was partially cooked in the crock-pot first and then I cut it into large strips, from there I followed the instructions above. The coating was crispy and had a great texture, but my batter was a bit thick and I found there were spots were it was a bit mushy under the outside crust after frying. Next time I would thin it out so it was more like waffle batter and less like drippy cookie dough and will cook evenly. Served these with waffles and corn and they were awesome! Would definitely make these again!!

This was the best fried chicken recipe I tried so far. I will continue to use this. Make sure you use enough paprika and you won't need extra spice. Instead of dipping it into 2 bowls I put the egg in one bowl and the flour mix in the other. Dipped in the egg, then flour and again, coating it twice. Super crispy! Also try to let the chicken sit for about 20 minutes before frying it. The coating will have a chance to set better to prevent it flying off.

The  SEARCH  IS NOW OVER !!!! This truly thePERFECT FRIED CHICKEN RECIPE EVER !!!
I have been experimenting  with  other recipes  for  YEARS (this  is not an EXAGGERATION) on Fried chicken but they did not come out so good. The coating in this recipes does not fall off when frying nor when taking it out,it most definitely does stay on.  I took some hints from  the other readers stating that the flour mixture was to bland so following the recipe I added in some more spices like my husband's Weber 
K C BBQ rub,long with just a dash of cumin, seasoned salt, and garlic powder instead of garlic salt. the suggested time for frying  and at  350 was just perfect , I cooked  the drumsticks at 350 for 18 minutes and the chicken came out a PICTURE PERFECT GOLDEN BROWN . I will definitely  will used this recipe again . 
P.S  I also used the article  here in  ALL RECIPES by  Carl Hanson on How To Fried Chicken and the tip about using  parchment paper and letting  the coating  sit for a little  while.

text:
I like mine with more spice, so next time I'll add some hot sauce to the wet mixture.  It was perfectly crispy, even the next day when I ate the leftovers cold.

I have a infrared thermometer that I checked my oil temp with.  Make sure it doesn't get above 400 because canola/peanut oil will start to smoke and give your chicken a rancid flavor.  Also try to keep the temp above 350, that keeps the oil from soaking into the breading and making it greasy.

Yesterday I marinated 9 chicken breast in the same spices. Today I googled "crispy fried chicken recipes" and clicked this one. Read some reviews and followed the recipe. Added an extra cup of flour, one extra egg yolk, tbsp of salt and used nearly all of a 12 oz bottle of Heineken beer. The house smells amazing and my husband keeps coming up from the garage to steal a taste. Our three yr is hard to please but she's following me around the kitchen for another taste. This recipe is the closest to the KFC flavor I've tried. Fam fav recipe for the books! Wouldn't fry chicken any other way! Thank you

This is by far my family's favorite fried chicken recipe. It's a great recipe, but personally I find it a bit bland. If you go heavy on the seasoning, it's better. Using a deep fryer makes the coating more uniform. I usually make a double batch of chicken strips with the batter. It's great on a salad for lunch the next day, or the kids eat it cold with dip.

Saw this come through in my email the other day - and since I've never been able to get a decent crunch to my chicken, definitely wanted to try this.

Awesome. Worked wonderfully. Used exact recipe minus just a little pepper as the gf is not into spicy foods.  Should have left it in, but will next time and maybe even ratchet it up a bit.  Also used boneless breasts sliced into half to thin them down a bit.  Had to cut down the oil temperature to about 300-325 to get the crust crunchy and brown properly without drying out the chicken.

This will be my NEW "go to" fried chicken!

I'm giving this a 4 instead of a 5 only because I found the gravy to be very bland until I doctored it up. The chicken was great, if you like it crispy this is the recipe to use, though I would suggest a bit more seasoning in the batter. To the gravy I added some salt and pepper and about 1/4 tsp each of thyme and sage. I also added about 1/2 tsp of Old Bay seasoning. With these additions the gravy was delicious. Next time I will also add some Old Bay to the batter for the chicken too.

city:

None
country:
None
text:
So delicious!

I do think the flour and batter mixtures were a bit much. I had a ton left over!

I used Pabst Blue Ribbon for the beer batter. Was the only beer I could find in a single can, and it worked well!

I would definitely add about 2 tbsp of cayenne instead of 1.

I recommend keeping the chicken out until it's close to room temperature. It's helps prevent the crust from burning and will cook at a more even rate. Do the larger cuts first like the breast and thighs--then about halfway in, toss in the drumsticks and wings. If you put all of it in at once, cooking will not be even because the meat will cool the oil down. Or you could do the larger cuts as the first batch, then the smaller cuts as a second batch. The larger cuts will still be pretty hot when the smaller cuts finish.

I would also use less beer/water than is suggested so you can get a creamier/thicker batter instead of runny.

text:
Made it as written the first time, and the chicken (boneless, skinless breasts cut into strips) came out juicy with the breading nice and crispy. I used my small deep fryer set to 350, and cooked two strips at a time for 9-10 minutes, keeping the done strips warm in 170 degree oven. BUT, the breading was bland and had no taste.

Second time, I doubled all the spices, but in place of garlic salt used garlic powder and salt separately, added 3T onion powder, 1t cayenne pepper, and used sage instead of poultry seasoning. I also added  a T salt to the wet mixture. It was perfect!

For those having trouble with the thickness of the wet mixture, use an entire 12 oz bottle of beer initially. Err on the side of it being too thin rather than too thick. As the dry mixture begins to thicken the wet, add a splash of beer at a time to thin it, and whisk again to incorporate the dry clumps.

country:
None
text:
Finally, fried chicken that gets & stays crispy after cooking off! 
I see alot of complaints about it being bland- the batter here has a decent flavor, it's your chicken itself that's bland. You need to brine your chicken for several hours first. Mix up a batch of brine (simply salt and water- try 1/4 cup or so salt dissolved in 2 -3 quartsof water depending on how much you need to cover the chicken) , soak your chicken pieces in it for about 1 1/2 -2 hours or so, drain, rinse and pat dry. If you want even more flavor, let sit in brine a bit longer next time.

text:
This is a very good recipe which makes a terrific crust, but flavoring the actual chicken has been neglected. What you want to do is, the day before, rinse and cut up the chicken into pieces. I have a large stainless stockpot into which I pour about a gallon of water, and then dissolve 3/4 cup of salt and 2 tsp. of Accent (msg) into it. Add the chicken and allow to marinate for a full 22 hours. Then just follow the recipe here and you've got yourself some real Southern fried chicken!

text:
Another opportunity to air my lessons learned.  First, make sure your chicken pieces are not too big.  I used combined leg/thighs as that is what I had on hand.  Should have separated them first.  The bigger the piece, the longer it will take to deep fry and the more over-done coating will be.  Get the picture?  I eventually started taking pieces out earlier when I thought coating looked good, and finished in oven.  Guess you could alternatively pre-cook in microwave.  But having smaller pieces would have likely prevented having to do either.  I may try again, now that I have learned this lesson.  But thought the final coating was a little too crispy...think outer shell

text:
OK - Wow! This was great.

The texture and crispiness of the finished product reminds me of the Hot and Spicy style KFC, without the heat. I followed the instructions  but personally, I would double all of the spices next time - and probably add even more salt. Oh and I added onion powder too, about 1/2TB. 

I used three joint chicken wings and just divided each joint, discarding the tips -so i had those half sized wing pieces,that's my favourite type of chicken to use when frying. 

I also did a buttermilk soak for about 20 mins before frying, so rather than wetting each piece with a bit of water before the 3 step dipping process, I just pulled mine straight out of the seasoned buttermilk and then hit the dry then wet then dry. 

I cannot recommend this recipe and process more highly! Thanks for this - I used cheap old 'blended vegetable oil' at $4 for 4 Litres and it worked a charm. I made about $60 worth of KFC in my own home for around $10 - you can't complain about that! Thank you so much for your recipe!

text:
I'm a simple man of simple tastes, so when my great aunt Gretchen suggested I partake in the culinary experience that is triple dipped chicken I was a little taken aback by her audacity.  As I scanned through the recipe outlined by the amateur  QUIRKYIQ my doubt for this dish only deepened.  The crass, almost insulting, way this excuse for a gourmet artisan hamfistedly drowned such pitiful amounts of garlic salt in an overwhelming sea of paprika called to mind an image of the great Michel Richard rolling over in his grave.  However, I respect nothing more than the culinary insight of my beloved Gretchen, so I threw caution to the wind and through gritted teeth prepared a dish of the so called "Triple Dipped Fried Chicken" for myself and my sweet ferret, Annabel.

It was pretty good, will make again.

text:
I made this chicken & it was absolutely delicious! The only poultry seasoning I had was an A-1 steak & poultry rub. I added some of that to the flour & I added season salt & I added more garlic salt than what is posted here. I basically seasoned to taste. I would dip my finger in the flour mixture & taste to see if it had the desired flavor. I also used water instead of beer. I have always seen chicken dipped in a flour mixture & in the eggs, but I've never seen the eggs mixed with flour, pepper, etc. It made the coat thicker & really gave the chicken a good crust. I will definitely make my fried chicken like this from now on! Thank you for sharing your wonderful recipe! =D

text:
I made this recipe at a cooking demo that I did today at the Lodge Factory Store in Commerce, GA. It was stellar!!! I in the wet mix, I used 1 Tbsp of salt instead of 1 tsp. Also in the wet mix I used beer - Yuengling Lager. It was absolutely perfect! I was making this chicken to be a part of another recipe, but the chicken on its own was amazing. One note - after dredging in the dry mixture for the second time, allow the chicken to rest before cooking until the dry mix forms a paste-like consistency. This creates crispier chicken with no residual flour in your oil. Very, very good recipe! I cannot recommend it enough!

text:
This was a decent basic recipe in need of some tweaking. I skipped the last dip into the flour, I just didn't feel like dealing with the mess. I used tenderloins and soaked them in buttermilk for about 30 minutes to get them juicy and tender. Three cups of flour seemed like such a waste, so only about 1 1/2 cups of seasoned flour were used. This batter is definitely crispy and I had no trouble getting it to stick to the chicken. Even after adding more spices, it seemed like something was missing. These would be great with some buffalo ranch dressing or honey mustard.

This was ok. While I was impressed with the batter, the chicken itself didn't taste very good. My husband said it was boring and my 6 yo ate only half of one drumstick. I might try the batter with chopped steaks, but probably won't use with chicken again. Thanks anyway.
